<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6012251206749099511">Sally is sixteen and uncommonly pretty. Her knowledge of English literature, French, history, art and music is non-existent, but she has a thorough grounding in military tactics, can run a business, ride like a Cossack and shoot straight with a pistol.<br /><br />When her dear father is drowned in suspicious circumstances in the South China Sea, Sally is left to fend for herself, an o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6012251206749099511">Sally is sixteen and uncommonly pretty. Her knowledge of English literature, French, history, art and music is non-existent, but she has a thorough grounding in military tactics, can run a business, ride like a Cossack and shoot straight with a pistol.<br /><br />When her dear father is drowned in suspicious circumstances in the South China Sea, Sally is left to fend for herself, an orphan and alone in the smoky fog of Victorian London. Though she doesn't know it, Sally is already in terrible danger. Soon the mystery and the danger will deepen - and at the rotten heart of it all lies the deadly secret of the ruby in the smoke...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6012251206749099511">...more</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_675431400">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/675431400" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday" class="left imgcol" title="mark monday"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446402303p2/131922.jpg" alt="mark monday" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/675431400?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 26, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday" class="user" title="mark monday">mark monday</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/64428.The_Ruby_In_The_Smoke" title="Paperback 9780439977784" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=foggy-nights" class="actionLinkLite">foggy-nights</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=teenworld" class="actionLinkLite">teenworld</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer675431400">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11169665314544461510">You know this smart and swiftly paced Victorian mystery is written for young adults, right? You know that doesn't mean dumbed down or raw, but rather that it should not be cluttered up with obtrusive literariness or head-scratching ephemera. You say that Pullman struggles with figurative language and that he doesn't find his own voice and I have to say... what exactly do you mean by 'figurative language' and how is he struggling with it? I saw no such struggle and I read a very specific voice. P</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11169665314544461510">You know this smart and swiftly paced Victorian mystery is written for young adults, right? You know that doesn't mean dumbed down or raw, but rather that it should not be cluttered up with obtrusive literariness or head-scratching ephemera. You say that Pullman struggles with figurative language and that he doesn't find his own voice and I have to say... what exactly do you mean by 'figurative language' and how is he struggling with it? I saw no such struggle and I read a very specific voice. Pullman pulls off a YA adventure without dumbing it down and his voice is clearly an intelligent and political and subtle one. perhaps too subtle? he up-ends various conventions of the genre: the heroine doesn't solve the mystery herself (it happens off-stage! highly unusual and refreshing and without melodrama); her skills are in accounting rather than detection; she lives in the Victorian era and all that implies regarding the status of women - yet she doesn't sigh or moon about wistfully over love, she doesn't stress about manners, she is forthright and intelligent and bold without becoming a unrealistic wish fulfillment version of a Victorian heroine. she fits perfectly within her time and still manages to stand out in her own particular way.<br /><br />You say the characters are flat and uninteresting; I say we must have read different books! the characters, both heroes &amp; villains, practically jumped off of the page for me, each one a tasty and compelling creation. there was a not-so-underlying theme of the importance of equality and one of the most clever ways that Pullman gets his point across is by bringing together an entirely disparate crew of well-realized supporting characters and making them all perform and interact as equals. that was a lovely thing to behold and it was made so heartwarming - yet without sickly sweet sentiment. the book makes equality feel like the most natural thing in the world. You thought the central villain was dull! that vicious old lady is one of the more memorable villains I've experienced in young adult fiction. mad, bad, and dangerous to know; cruel and cunning and given a particularly surprising and compelling backstory. You say the heroine isn't much of a role model; I must beg to differ! sure she does a questionable thing or two - does she need to be perfect? don't challenging times mean a person has to do a challenging thing or two, something they very well may regret? is it the opium that bothered you? well it bothered me too - just as it clearly was intended. England's sickening role in the opium trade with China bothers me and it certainly bothers the author; thus no punches are pulled. I applaud that. did you not understand that you were actually picking up a book by Phillip Pullman and not by the Lollipop Guild?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11169665314544461510">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_39743448">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39743448" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1775247-larissa" class="left imgcol" title="Larissa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1380050552p2/1775247.jpg" alt="Larissa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/39743448?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 09, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1775247-larissa" class="user" title="Larissa">Larissa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/64428.The_Ruby_In_The_Smoke" title="Paperback 9780439977784" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Yes</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Larissa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/87345-jenna">Jenna</a>
  </div>



    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39743448">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13181758020397006315">With a subtitle of "A Sally Lockhart Mystery," one might expect the first installment of said series to be about a girl who restores pinched puppies to their rightful dowdy owners. And you wouldn't be more wrong! The Ruby in the Smoke introduces Sally, a self-made woman already at 16 years old, with an accidental death and a call to action. Her father has died under mysterious circumstances, and it's up to her (and eventually a merry, ragtag band of comrades including an equally quickwitted youn</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13181758020397006315">With a subtitle of "A Sally Lockhart Mystery," one might expect the first installment of said series to be about a girl who restores pinched puppies to their rightful dowdy owners. And you wouldn't be more wrong! The Ruby in the Smoke introduces Sally, a self-made woman already at 16 years old, with an accidental death and a call to action. Her father has died under mysterious circumstances, and it's up to her (and eventually a merry, ragtag band of comrades including an equally quickwitted young photographer) to avenge his death and put a whole host of non-puppy related things to rights.<br /><br />What's more, the books are set in 19th century London. This makes the book extra-engaging for two reasons: <br /><br />1.) Sally's quick-thinking, independent woman ways get her branded a heathen from the very start. It makes it harder for her to succeed in any endeavor outside of lacing up a corset, and when she does tenfold it's all the more cheer-worthy and inspiring. <br /><br />2.) Old timeyness factor! Peeps be wearing waistcoats.<br /><br />Overall, this is a fantastic start to a series about the strength found in resourcefulness, self-discipline, and friendship forged on the path to bringing down a wicked opium lord.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13181758020397006315">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_39384368">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39384368" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1777976-lorcon" class="left imgcol" title="LorCon"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1230668799p2/1777976.jpg" alt="LorCon" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/39384368?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 18, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1777976-lorcon" class="user" title="LorCon">LorCon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1777976-lorcon?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39384368">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1703413712705784924">I'm a big fan of Pullman's His Dark Materials trilogy, so I thought I would give this a try. Heck, I even liked the Golden Compass movie (two words--Daniel Craig). This is what librarians call "young adult" literature i.e. "for teenagers." As such, I find it a bit disturbing. I'm a far cry from a book-burning censor but this heroine is not my idea of a role model. Set in Victorian London, Sally Lockhart is an orphan (of course)who falls in with a Dickensian cast of characters to solve her father</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1703413712705784924">I'm a big fan of Pullman's His Dark Materials trilogy, so I thought I would give this a try. Heck, I even liked the Golden Compass movie (two words--Daniel Craig). This is what librarians call "young adult" literature i.e. "for teenagers." As such, I find it a bit disturbing. I'm a far cry from a book-burning censor but this heroine is not my idea of a role model. Set in Victorian London, Sally Lockhart is an orphan (of course)who falls in with a Dickensian cast of characters to solve her father's murder. She packs a pistol and dabbles with opium, but has to get a man to purchase them for her. It doesn't even occur to her to try to solve the riddle...she's too busy embarking on a career as an accountant! She's also rather too quick to tell all her secrets to everyone she meets. And pretty much everyone ends up conveniently dead. Oh, dear. Where is Nancy Drew when we need her? Pullman should stick to insulting religion.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1703413712705784924">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14665764594031242246">Sally Lockhart is an orphan during the 1879s in London. She begins to discover the truth about her father, while being menaced by some very creepy characters.<br /><br />I enjoyed this far more than the Golden Compass books, as the narrative wasn't marred by the high whine of Pullman's anti-Narnia axe being ground.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText14665764594031242246">Sally Lockhart is an orphan during the 1879s in London. She begins to discover the truth about her father, while being menaced by some very creepy characters.<br /><br />I enjoyed this far more than the Golden Compass books, as the narrative wasn't marred by the high whine of Pullman's anti-Narnia axe being ground. The narrative voice dips into condescension here and there, but that actually fits period literature for younger readers, and the atmosphere of London's darker reaches was vivid and evocative.<br /><br />It was a fun three hour read, but didn't leave me with the desire to search out more, though if they come my way I will.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_400109855">

  <a href="/user/show/5105002-peter" class="left imgcol" title="Peter"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448640054p2/5105002.jpg" alt="Peter" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/400109855?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 16, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5105002-peter" class="user" title="Peter">Peter</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5105002-peter?shelf=victorians" class="actionLinkLite">victorians</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5105002-peter?shelf=london" class="actionLinkLite">london</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5105002-peter?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5105002-peter?shelf=read-2012" class="actionLinkLite">read-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer400109855">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5069202701490770838">I'm a big fan of 'His Dark Materials' and 'Ruby in the Smoke' is set in a similar Victorian world, but without the steampunk or magical elements. It's a murder mystery where teenage orphan Sally Lockhart searches for her father's killer and tries to discover his connection to the Ruby of the title and the significance of his last warning to her - 'Beware the seven blessings.' <br /><br />At around 200 pages it was a quick read. The writing is not quite as sophisticated as 'His Dark Materials', but is still</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5069202701490770838">I'm a big fan of 'His Dark Materials' and 'Ruby in the Smoke' is set in a similar Victorian world, but without the steampunk or magical elements. It's a murder mystery where teenage orphan Sally Lockhart searches for her father's killer and tries to discover his connection to the Ruby of the title and the significance of his last warning to her - 'Beware the seven blessings.' <br /><br />At around 200 pages it was a quick read. The writing is not quite as sophisticated as 'His Dark Materials', but is still really good and captures the Victorian turn of phrase very well. I can see some Dickensian influence and I imagine a bit from Wilkie Collins and Conan Doyle too. Occasionally there were a few last minute liberties written into the story to make things work - suddenly discovering Frederick is an expert climber is one that springs to mind and there was another one that was to do with the ruby. The villain Mrs Holland is a great character, but unlike Mrs Coulter, I didn't quite buy the web of influence and power she seemed to have accrued. There were also lots of good London locations and secondary characters. I will definitely read the next one in the series.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5069202701490770838">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_189777102">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/189777102" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/84023-j-g-keely" class="left imgcol" title="J.G. Keely"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1274333636p2/84023.jpg" alt="J.G. Keely" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/189777102?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 09, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/84023-j-g-keely" class="user" title="J.G. Keely">J.G. Keely</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=novel" class="actionLinkLite">novel</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=uk-and-ireland" class="actionLinkLite">uk-and-ireland</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer189777102">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17832969262458971954">I always find myself frustrated when authors can't seem to think of anything bad for their characters to overcome, and so they have to create some unbelievably vindictive and amoral villain just so there is some central conflict. The main character gets along with everyone and always finds satisfying solutions to any momentary setback.<br /><br />The only problems such super-protagonists can't solve are those which they don't yet know the details of, so Pullman gives us a faux-mystery to keep the character</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17832969262458971954">I always find myself frustrated when authors can't seem to think of anything bad for their characters to overcome, and so they have to create some unbelievably vindictive and amoral villain just so there is some central conflict. The main character gets along with everyone and always finds satisfying solutions to any momentary setback.<br /><br />The only problems such super-protagonists can't solve are those which they don't yet know the details of, so Pullman gives us a faux-mystery to keep the character in the dark, but requires too many leaps for the reader to be able to puzzle things out. Then, he has one of the secondary characters wrap the entire thing up offstage near the climax.<br /><br />This was especially bothersome because he just threw out all of the lead-up (i.e., the mystery), and instead gave us a climax which had little to do with anything previous in the book.<br /><br />Pullman's writing was just as raw as his plotting, and you could see him struggling to use figurative language. In the end, he never finds a solid voice, and most of his characters end up as rather predictable placeholders.<br /><br />It wasn't a bad book, and it had its moments, here and there, but it lifted its plot from the seminal mystery story, <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17663593">The Moonstone</a>, and in all other regards seemed to be aping Kipling and Conrad.<br /><br />Not that those are bad sources from which to take inspiration, but Pullman isn't doing anything new here, nor does he demonstrate the florid voice and sense of character which made those authors stand out. He tries to overcome this by giving us of little details about Victorian London, but most of them are just bits of geography, and one never gets a sense of the amazing, alien place evoked by Mayhew's <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_Labour_and_the_London_Poor">London Poor</a>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17832969262458971954">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_10623964">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10623964" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/635443-ana-t" class="left imgcol" title="Ana T."><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1204313983p2/635443.jpg" alt="Ana T." /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/10623964?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 05, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/635443-ana-t" class="user" title="Ana T.">Ana T.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/847487.The_Ruby_In_The_Smoke" title="Paperback 9780439943666" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/635443-ana-t?shelf=read-in-2008" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer10623964">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13080999479180600867">I started this book with great expectation having heard so much about Pullman and his His Dark Materials books. Besides it is set in Victorian London and I love those stories.<br /><br />Have you ever heard the phrase The Seven Blessings? <br />That question causes a man to die of shock, and propels Sally Lockhart into a desperate adventure that will expose the deepest secrets of the corrupt and murderous opium trade. <br />Sally is sixteen when the story begins, orphaned and alone. She's had an unconventional educatio</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13080999479180600867">I started this book with great expectation having heard so much about Pullman and his His Dark Materials books. Besides it is set in Victorian London and I love those stories.<br /><br />Have you ever heard the phrase The Seven Blessings? <br />That question causes a man to die of shock, and propels Sally Lockhart into a desperate adventure that will expose the deepest secrets of the corrupt and murderous opium trade. <br />Sally is sixteen when the story begins, orphaned and alone. She's had an unconventional education: her knowledge of English Literature, French, History, Art and Music is non-existent, but she has a thorough grounding in military tactics, can run a business, ride like a Cossack and shoot straight with a pistol. When her father is drowned in suspicious circumstances in the South China Sea, Sally soon finds herself in terrible danger too - and at the rotten heart of it all lies the deadly secret of the ruby in the smoke.<br /><br />I found he has a great way to describe characters and setting, I could almost see Sally and the Garlands and Mrs Holland going about the streets of London. However I think there were some problems with the plot. It's supposedly a mystery however I never felt a suspense thrill, it mentions opium dens and shady characters but only in some few selected scenes did I feel that dark atmosphere. Sally never really interested me much, she is supposedly the sleuth that is going to discover everything but I felt that we get as much information from the villains if not more than from Sally. She was more worried in trying to remember the past and to know why her father was killed than actually looking for the lost ruby or helping save Adelaide when that was needed. I could never really warm up to her. On the other hand I really liked Jim and Rosa and would really like to know what happened to Adelaide.<br /><br />The bad guys are really bad, namely the infamous Mrs Holland but it seems she manages to hurt everybody except Sally, who is supposedly the real target! Isn't that odd? Besides the story is slowly revealed, at times too slowly and then in the last chapters everything is solved with a nicely thought twist to explain everything and every character involved. <br /><br />It seems to me that the idea behind the story was a good one (I keep thinking of Emilio Salgari's stories because of the indian bad guys and the famous cursed jewel) but somehow the final result is not as good as it should be.<br /><br />Grade: C+</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13080999479180600867">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_75477703">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75477703" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/50378-angie" class="left imgcol" title="Angie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1260221213p2/50378.jpg" alt="Angie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/75477703?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/50378-angie" class="user" title="Angie">Angie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=good-uns" class="actionLinkLite">good-uns</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=nostalgireads" class="actionLinkLite">nostalgireads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=girls-who-do-things" class="actionLinkLite">girls-who-do-things</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=ya" class="actionLinkLite">ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer75477703">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4928437975963221175">I remember buying my copy of THE RUBY IN THE SMOKE at a B. Dalton bookstore in San Antonio, Texas. I liked the cover with the young girl in the cape holding something mysterious in a white handkerchief for a slightly creepy old woman to inspect. But, in the end, this was yet another example of a book I bought for the opening lines alone.<br /><blockquote>On a cold, fretful afternoon in early October, 1872, a hansom cab drew up outside the offices of Lockhart and Selby, Shipping Agents, in the financial heart of L</blockquote></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4928437975963221175">I remember buying my copy of THE RUBY IN THE SMOKE at a B. Dalton bookstore in San Antonio, Texas. I liked the cover with the young girl in the cape holding something mysterious in a white handkerchief for a slightly creepy old woman to inspect. But, in the end, this was yet another example of a book I bought for the opening lines alone.<br /><blockquote>On a cold, fretful afternoon in early October, 1872, a hansom cab drew up outside the offices of Lockhart and Selby, Shipping Agents, in the financial heart of London, and a young girl got out and paid the driver.<br /> She was a person of sixteen or so--alone, and uncommonly pretty. She was slender and pale, and dressed in mourning, with a black bonnet under which she tucked back a straying twist of blond hair that the wind had teased loose. She had unusually dark brown eyes for one so fair. Her name was Sally Lockhart; and within fifteen minutes, she was going to kill a man.</blockquote><br />Yeah, there was sort of no way my 12-year-old self wasn't going to make a beeline to the cash register with that one. All I knew was that it was set in Victorian London, it was a mystery, and it clearly featured a girl I wanted to get to know better. I had no idea it was the first in a trilogy, or how involved I would become in the incredibly intricate plot that stretches out over all three books. It should be noted that Pullman published a fourth volume almost ten years after THE RUBY IN THE SMOKE, but it is less of a direct sequel and more a companion novel to the original trilogy.<br /><br />Sally Lockhart is so very far from your average 16-year-old. Even your average 16-year-old in 19th century London. Her father has recently been murdered and she is intent on uncovering the identity of his killer and bringing the villain to justice. As such, she comes to his offices in London to meet with his partner and find out if he knows anything about Mr. Lockhart's demise or the phrase, "Beware the seven blessings," which she came across in a fragment of a letter sent to her from Singapore. Shortly after her arrival she becomes embroiled in another murder, the vagaries of the opium trade, and the mystery of the disappearance of the fabled Ruby of Agrapur. Along the way she encounters a few associates who become true friends, including a young scarecrow of an errand boy named Jim Taylor and an amiable photographer by the name of Frederick Garland. She will have need of her friends before the game is played out and she races against the clock to make sense of her convoluted past and discover just who is behind the strange web of betrayal and deceit that has taken over her life.<br /><br />Everyone is familiar with <a title="Philip Pullman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3618.Philip_Pullman">Philip Pullman</a>'s much more famous <a title="The Golden Compass (His Dark Materials, Book 1) by Philip Pullman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/119322.The_Golden_Compass__His_Dark_Materials__Book_1_">His Dark Materials</a> trilogy. I snatched up the first book when it came out because I was already a huge Pullman fan because of the Sally Lockhart books. And I enjoyed <a title="The Golden Compass (His Dark Materials, Book 1) by Philip Pullman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/119322.The_Golden_Compass__His_Dark_Materials__Book_1_">The Golden Compass</a> just fine. But I got halfway through <a title="His Dark Materials Trilogy (The Golden Compass; The Subtle Knife; The Amber Spyglass) by Philip Pullman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18116.His_Dark_Materials_Trilogy__The_Golden_Compass__The_Subtle_Knife__The_Amber_Spyglass_">The Subtle Knife</a> and the whole thing just...petered out for me. I'm still not exactly sure what happened except that I kept wishing the entire time I was reading about Sally instead. But in my experience few people have read this set of excellent mysteries. They are dark, dire, and grim, to be sure. But they are also absolutely delightful. And bite-your-nails-to-the-quick intense. Sally herself is such a strong character--a perfect blend of independence, diffidence, integrity, and intelligence. Following her growth and development over the course of the trilogy is an absolutely moving experience. Each book matures in both subject matter and length. THE RUBY IN THE SMOKE reads like Dickens meets Arthur Conan Doyle meets Lloyd Alexander and that combination proved too charming for me to resist. I could not put it down until I finished it and I immediately went out and bought the next two books. They did not disappoint, but rather ratcheted up the stakes with each passing page. Pullman somehow manages to create the atmosphere of a vintage penny dreadful, while peopling it with fully fleshed out characters who work their way seamlessly into the reader's heart and affections. In fact, I vividly remember breaking down sobbing while reading a certain scene in the second book--<a title="The Shadow in the North (Sally Lockhart Trilogy, Book 2) by Philip Pullman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/210919.The_Shadow_in_the_North__Sally_Lockhart_Trilogy__Book_2_">The Shadow in the North</a>. It is one of my very first memories of connecting with a set of characters so much it was physically painful to me to watch them suffer. An engrossing series highly recommended, particularly for fans of <a title="Libba Bray" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2526.Libba_Bray">Libba Bray</a>'s Gemma Doyle trilogy and <a title="Laurie R. King" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6760.Laurie_R__King">Laurie R. King</a>'s Mary Russell series.<br />Reading order: THE RUBY IN THE SMOKE, <a title="The Shadow in the North (Sally Lockhart Trilogy, Book 2) by Philip Pullman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/210919.The_Shadow_in_the_North__Sally_Lockhart_Trilogy__Book_2_">The Shadow in the North</a>, and <a title="The Tiger in the Well (Sally Lockhart Trilogy, Book 3) by Philip Pullman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/210918.The_Tiger_in_the_Well__Sally_Lockhart_Trilogy__Book_3_">The Tiger in the Well</a>. Companion novel: <a title="The Tin Princess by Philip Pullman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/87273.The_Tin_Princess">The Tin Princess</a>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4928437975963221175">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rhiannon by: </span>
      The January Pick - Forever Young Adult's Boston Bookclub

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/5071150-rhiannon?shelf=i-suck-at-using-the-library" class="actionLinkLite">i-suck-at-using-the-library</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5071150-rhiannon?shelf=i-love-this-author" class="actionLinkLite">i-love-this-author</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5071150-rhiannon?shelf=dont-forget-to-buy-this-someday" class="actionLinkLite">dont-forget-to-buy-this-someday</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer246669928">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8120179703762052019">Philip Pullman might have the biggest pair of <strong>balls</strong> in YA Lit. In my first foray into Pullman's work, he killed God and encouraged teen sex to heal the world. In <em>The Ruby In The Smoke: A Sally Lockhart Mystery</em>, his teenage heroine is encouraged to use drugs to fill in the plot-holes of her life, and she shoots and kills an evil pirate, with a gun she had locked and loaded in her handbag. Lolz - love it!<br /><br />The setting of <em>The Ruby...</em> is perhaps my favorite setting ever: Victorian London. The East End</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8120179703762052019">Philip Pullman might have the biggest pair of <strong>balls</strong> in YA Lit. In my first foray into Pullman's work, he killed God and encouraged teen sex to heal the world. In <em>The Ruby In The Smoke: A Sally Lockhart Mystery</em>, his teenage heroine is encouraged to use drugs to fill in the plot-holes of her life, and she shoots and kills an evil pirate, with a gun she had locked and loaded in her handbag. Lolz - love it!<br /><br />The setting of <em>The Ruby...</em> is perhaps my favorite setting ever: Victorian London. The East End, Wapping, The Seven Dials - been there before in <em>real</em> Victorian novels - and this felt just as authentic to me as it did when I was reading the literature of the period. (In fact, because of this book, I can't get the setting out of my head, and have followed with <em>Jonathan Strange &amp; Mr Norrell</em>).<br /><br />As you might expect, there are several Victorian-y or "Dickensian" moments in <em>The Ruby...</em>, including some very lucky coincidences and an inheritance plot. This was a very enjoyable read...but, it's hard to imagine a young-YA feeling the vibe of this ultimately-kind-of-dark mystery. Tell you what though - I'd want to hang out with the totally-rad-<em>actual</em>-YA that did read the Sally Lockhart mysteries...Yeah, we'd be friends...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8120179703762052019">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_38102180">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38102180" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1256101-michael-ames" class="left imgcol" title="Michael Ames"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1398657715p2/1256101.jpg" alt="Michael Ames" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/38102180?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 01, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1256101-michael-ames" class="user" title="Michael Ames">Michael Ames</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38102180">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10504102199780238466">This book is a refreshing departure for Philip Pullman, for those of us who are only acquainted with <a title=" His Dark Materials" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20His%20Dark%20Materials"> His Dark Materials</a>. It's a great mystery, immediately engaging with authentic, realistic characters and settings. I'd recommend it for adults and mature teenagers with a taste for dark mystery. I'll read the next one. <br /><br />In fact, the only reason I can't give this book four stars is that parents need to be very cautious about the age and emotional maturity of children who read it. The Ruby in the Sm</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10504102199780238466">This book is a refreshing departure for Philip Pullman, for those of us who are only acquainted with <a title=" His Dark Materials" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20His%20Dark%20Materials"> His Dark Materials</a>. It's a great mystery, immediately engaging with authentic, realistic characters and settings. I'd recommend it for adults and mature teenagers with a taste for dark mystery. I'll read the next one. <br /><br />In fact, the only reason I can't give this book four stars is that parents need to be very cautious about the age and emotional maturity of children who read it. The Ruby in the Smoke deals heavily with opium use and ultimately condemns it in no uncertain terms; however, the message gets clouded when the heroin (puns intended) deliberately uses the drug and achieves only positive outcomes. <br /><br />Mature readers will easily place these events in their proper context and the book's much stronger theme of the destructive nature of opium will prevail. But in my opinion, in spite of often being billed as children's books, this and Pullman's other works are better suited for adults.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10504102199780238466">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_893296240">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/893296240" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/19129334-kerry-hunter" class="left imgcol" title="Kerry Hunter"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1444204865p2/19129334.jpg" alt="Kerry Hunter" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/893296240?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 04, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19129334-kerry-hunter" class="user" title="Kerry Hunter">Kerry Hunter</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/64428.The_Ruby_In_The_Smoke" title="Paperback 9780439977784" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/19129334-kerry-hunter?shelf=2014" class="actionLinkLite">2014</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19129334-kerry-hunter?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer893296240">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8992744437523056465">Throughout the year of 2014, I told myself I'd re-read some of my favourite books from my childhood. This was the first one I picked up as I remember being absolutely addicted to the series way back when. It was just as incredible as I remembered, maybe even more so thanks to finally catching the adult themes and jokes within the book within my adult eyes.<br /><br />What do a man drowning at sea, a heart attack victim and a mysterious message all have in common? Little Sally Lockheart. That's all I'm going</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8992744437523056465">Throughout the year of 2014, I told myself I'd re-read some of my favourite books from my childhood. This was the first one I picked up as I remember being absolutely addicted to the series way back when. It was just as incredible as I remembered, maybe even more so thanks to finally catching the adult themes and jokes within the book within my adult eyes.<br /><br />What do a man drowning at sea, a heart attack victim and a mysterious message all have in common? Little Sally Lockheart. That's all I'm going to say in regards to the premise of the book. You really do all have to read it and I don't want to give anything away. Even the slightest of details can hint at the final ending of the book.<br /><br />Philip Pullman really is the master storyteller. He keeps things succinct, and yet detailed, explained and yet exciting, and everything ties in with everything else almost far too perfectly. The language he uses is rich and inviting and always urges you to read "just one more" chapter. The heroine is amazing at some things, and yet does have her flaws, which I think makes her just that much more real. Instead of having a mastermind perfect at everything running an investigation, you have a flawed person investigating equally flawed people and so on. One of the main themes of this book is what some people call "the grey area". Not one person or object within this book is either good or evil, they always lie somewhere in between. I love that.<br /><br />The plot is engaging and unique and although everything is tied up neatly at the end, there are some loose threads that aren't explained which makes you want to read the next few books in the series. As if you wouldn't want to anyway, Philip Pullman is a genius. He always has, is, and will always remain, one of my favourite authors of all time.<br /><br />I salute you, my friend. I salute you.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8992744437523056465">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/2793431-lance-greenfield" class="user" title="Lance Greenfield">Lance Greenfield</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer306441381">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2778162394005146272">This is the first Sally Lockhart story that I have read, and it probably won't be the last.<br /><br />In the beginning, it was difficult for me to believe in the strength and forthrightness of this sixteen year old. She shows maturity well beyond her years. However, the more that I followed Sally around the streets of London, the more convincing she was, and the more that I lived her dangerous adventures alongside her.<br /><br />There are some very kind and generous characters in this book, and they form strong allia</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2778162394005146272">This is the first Sally Lockhart story that I have read, and it probably won't be the last.<br /><br />In the beginning, it was difficult for me to believe in the strength and forthrightness of this sixteen year old. She shows maturity well beyond her years. However, the more that I followed Sally around the streets of London, the more convincing she was, and the more that I lived her dangerous adventures alongside her.<br /><br />There are some very kind and generous characters in this book, and they form strong alliances with Sally to eventually get to the truth behind the mysteries surrounding the death of her sea-faring father. There are also some very dark and frightening characters, not least the daunting and evil Mrs Holland.<br /><br />It is interesting to read about the practicalities of early commercial photography, and about the London of over a century ago, although some things haven't changed!<br /><br />Throughout the book, Pullman maintains an air of tension and keeps events moving along at a fast pace. There are a lot of violent deaths splattered throughout the book, but they just add to the fear factor.<br /><br />Sally is such a resourceful and intelligent young lady. She sometimes survices by the skin of her teeth, but that is due to a combination of her own wits and the assistance of her good friends.<br /><br />A great adventure and a terrific ending!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2778162394005146272">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer526996599">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11677110254817416755">Originally reviewed on <a rel="nofollow" href="http://thebooksmugglers.com/2013/02/old-school-wednesdays-a-man-lay-dead-cocaine-blues-the-ruby-in-the-smoke.html">The Book Smugglers</a><br /><br />Sally Lockhart is sixteen years old when she loses her father. The only child of a successful merchant with a business of importing goods from far-off destinations, Sally is devastated when she learns that her father's boat has capsized somewhere off the coast of Singapore, killing him and every other soul onboard. To make matters worse, her only living relation is a distant, scornful Aunt, and her inheritance is far less than what it should be, thanks to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11677110254817416755">Originally reviewed on <a rel="nofollow" href="http://thebooksmugglers.com/2013/02/old-school-wednesdays-a-man-lay-dead-cocaine-blues-the-ruby-in-the-smoke.html">The Book Smugglers</a><br /><br />Sally Lockhart is sixteen years old when she loses her father. The only child of a successful merchant with a business of importing goods from far-off destinations, Sally is devastated when she learns that her father's boat has capsized somewhere off the coast of Singapore, killing him and every other soul onboard. To make matters worse, her only living relation is a distant, scornful Aunt, and her inheritance is far less than what it should be, thanks to a complication in her father's will. But what has Sally truly flummoxed is a mysterious, misspelled anonymous note she receives in the post, with the message: "Sali beware of the seven blessings. Marchbanks will help chattum. Bware darling." <br /><br />Little does Sally know that her quest to understand this message, to figure out what the mysterious Seven Blessings are, who Marchbanks is, will lead to devastating revelations about her past. Her quest for answers will also lead to a mysterious ruby, and a single-minded old woman who will stop at nothing to get her hands on this prize. <br /><br />Dear readers, I am incredibly remiss - I cannot believe that it took me so long to first discover that this book existed, and second, to actually read and review it. <em>The Ruby in the Smoke</em> is admittedly no His Dark Materials, but it is a wonderfully written and executed Victorian Mystery. And it's one I enjoyed very, very much. From the onset of the book (really, from the first paragraph introducing Sally Lockhart), I fell in love with the characters and the writing, with its universal omniscient - aka, the "Little Did She Know" foreshadowing/opinion - style. Instead of forced or affected, this writing choice feels very much like a Victorian novel, and imbues a sly character to the narration and some effective foreshadowing for twists to come as Sally and her friends unravel the mystery of the Maharajah's (cursed) missing ruby. On that note, the plot and true mystery angle of the novel is solid and executed perfectly. There are dual mysteries here, really, whose answers lie in Sally's past: the mystery of Sally's father's death (and the "seven blessings"), the mystery of the missing ruby (and the reasons why people desire it). Sally's first adventure is a story filled with secrets and reveals, with sojourns to isolated run down mansions, secret journals and hidden letters, opium dens and even pirates. Needless to say, there is a <em>lot</em> going on in <em>The Ruby in the Smoke</em>, but it never feels over-much or over-wrought - no small feat.<br /><br />On a character front, this book also excels. I <em>adore</em> Sally Lockhart, who is a no-nonsense heroine, who has no knowledge of French or literature but knows how to balance accounts, invest in stocks and bonds, and manage a business. (On that note, can I please interject - A HEROINE THAT LOVES MATH AND ECONOMICS! YES! THIS! I freaking love it!) In addition to the smart, steady-handed and sympathetic heroine we have in Sally, we also meet a swath of different characters, villains and friends alike, over the course of this book. Mrs. Holland, the book's villain, is a terrifying figure, with her cruelty (and the frightening image of her over-large, vicious dentures) and her singular desire to seize the ruby at any cost. We never really know what drives Mrs. Holland until the end of the book, when we learn a little more about her past and her character - she's no sympathetic villain, but she has a believable backstory that fuels her misery and obsession. <br /><br />The best characters, in my opinion, are the new friends that Sally makes - Jim, an apprentice clerk at Sally's shipping company with his keen insights (fueled by his love for penny dreadfuls); Frederick, the photographer who is terrible with numbers but passionate about his <em>art</em> (and who is quite taken with young Sally); Rosa, the vivacious, beautiful actress who has defied her family and spurned her inheritance for freedom and passion; and Adelaide, the urchin forced to do Mrs. Holland's bidding, but who finally finds friends and a brighter future. In sum, Sally has made a crew of friends with the perfect set of skills for a new investigation agency. I'm keen to see what happens in their next adventure together.<br /><br />Finally, I cannot end this review without saying something about that ending! I admit to tearing up just a little bit with that emotional final discovery, and I cannot wait to read the next book in this wonderful series. Absolutely recommended.<br /><br />(And clearly I must check out the 2006 BBC television adaptation - starring Billie Piper and Matt Smith in a strange out-of-sequence Doctor Who confluence of awesomeness?)<br /><br /><strong>Notable Quotes/Parts:</strong> From Chapter 1, the best introduction to a character, EVER:<br /><blockquote>On a cold, fretful afternoon in early October, 1872, a hansom cab drew up outside the offices of Lockhart and Selby, Shipping Agents, in the financial heart of London, and a young girl got out and paid the driver.<br /><br />She was a person of sixteen or so--alone, and uncommonly pretty. She was slender and pale, and dressed in mourning, with a black bonnet under which she tucked back a straying twist of blond hair that the wind had teased loose. She had unusually dark brown eyes for one so fair. Her name was Sally Lockhart; and within fifteen minutes, she was going to kill a man.</blockquote><br /><br /><strong>Rating: 7 - Very Good</strong></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11677110254817416755">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_678552239">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/678552239" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7232207-fiona" class="left imgcol" title="Fiona"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1424278621p2/7232207.jpg" alt="Fiona" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/678552239?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 20, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7232207-fiona" class="user" title="Fiona">Fiona</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7232207-fiona?shelf=young-adult-and-teen" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult-and-teen</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7232207-fiona?shelf=read-in-2013" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7232207-fiona?shelf=the-past" class="actionLinkLite">the-past</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7232207-fiona?shelf=i-taught-this-book" class="actionLinkLite">i-taught-this-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer678552239">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13451129909684311337">Hold your horses, everyone, the twenty-something nostalgia has set in. I’m noticing a couple of good, classic books for youngsters working their way back under my fictional radar in the last few months. I read <em> Ruby in the Smoke</em> when I was about twelve or thirteen, probably lured by the promise of Victorians, intrigue and lady-heroes who are good at accountancy. (I was that kind of child. My private games tended to involve a pencil and paper and the question “How would I run this as a self-suppo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13451129909684311337">Hold your horses, everyone, the twenty-something nostalgia has set in. I’m noticing a couple of good, classic books for youngsters working their way back under my fictional radar in the last few months. I read <em> Ruby in the Smoke</em> when I was about twelve or thirteen, probably lured by the promise of Victorians, intrigue and lady-heroes who are good at accountancy. (I was that kind of child. My private games tended to involve a pencil and paper and the question “How would I run this as a self-supporting enterprise?”) When lately it occurred to me that a story idea I’ve been playing with very much harks back to this, I thought I’d pick up a second-hand copy and see if I liked it as much as I remembered.<br /><br />This is a book for my hypothetical future daughter, for a start. Sally Lockhart is a fabulous heroine. She’s independent and can look out for herself, but she is not particularly streetwise or rebellious or ‘spunky’, and that’s okay. She’s got business acumen and staying power but she believes the best of people and makes a quiet virtue of treating them well. She’s not got weird-coloured hair or special skills, she’s neither exceptionally well-provided for nor rags-and-scraps poor, she’s not a chosen one in any way. She doesn’t sound like a YA heroine, or at least not the ones I’ve read. She sounds, in my head, a bit like younger me. Naturally I think she’s marvellous and I want my hypothetical future daughter to understand that good book-keeping and cheerfully volunteering to help with things are also character traits that can go with being a hero. Also that if you are going to smoke things, there is a clever way to do it and there is a not-clever way to do it.<br /><br />The main villain is genuinely creepy, and gets through dim-witted sidekicks at an alarming rate. She made a better villain before her reasons were explained – why are they so often so disappointing? Is it just that when we know a villain’s reasons for acting, they cease to be part of that ominous dark cloud of mystery in our imaginations? – but if I were Philip Pullman, I would have saved the final reveal (in the cab) for a different book. Or at least strung it out a bit. It was a little anticlimactic. Another thirty pages to build it up into something I cared about a little more, and this might have got bumped up another star.<br /><br />I just like anonymous notes and questing and housebreaking in search of mysterious papers and Baker Street Irregulars and people dropping dead in solicitors’ offices. I like sixteen year olds who know how to clean a pistol and also to negotiate contracts. I like scruffy photographers who wouldn’t get away with being such a low-key sort-of-vaguely love interest if this had been written in 2013, not 1987. I like pirates and Victorian-melodrama-shadowy-villainous-foreigners. This book did not knock me for six. But I enjoyed the hell out of it, and after some of the other stuff I’ve been reading of late, it is nice to dive straight back into the middle of my comfort zone and romp around for a bit.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13451129909684311337">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1159414796">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1159414796" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/38509278-sonja" class="left imgcol" title="Sonja"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1447062761p2/38509278.jpg" alt="Sonja" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1159414796?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 14, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/38509278-sonja" class="user" title="Sonja">Sonja</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/64428.The_Ruby_In_The_Smoke" title="Paperback 9780439977784" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who wish for their braincells to commit suicide</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1159414796">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18098661051738964349">The Ruby In The Smoke's central mystery is established at a breakneck speed in the first 30 pages or so, and this I do not mean in a positive sense. The plot, both poorly set up and rife with unbelievable coincidences, centres around a group of flat characters, introducing them too quickly and too superficially to become attached to them in any way. <br /><br />It is also full of holes. Plenty of the protagonists are made out to be keen of wit, yet, even with a plethora of bad guys on their heels, just wait</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18098661051738964349">The Ruby In The Smoke's central mystery is established at a breakneck speed in the first 30 pages or so, and this I do not mean in a positive sense. The plot, both poorly set up and rife with unbelievable coincidences, centres around a group of flat characters, introducing them too quickly and too superficially to become attached to them in any way. <br /><br />It is also full of holes. Plenty of the protagonists are made out to be keen of wit, yet, even with a plethora of bad guys on their heels, just waiting for knowledge of their whereabouts to kill them, they manage to all consider it a great idea to take stereographs of themselves for the sole purpose of selling them to the greater public. Plot "twists" and conflicts can be seen coming from miles away, and the final, major twist was so unnecessary as to put the moon coming out at noon to shame.<br /><br />Protagonist Sally is a 16 year old girl, complete with all the insecurities and difficulties that age brings. Yet these find only passing mention in the narrative, and have no bearing on the plot whatsoever. Instead, we have our attention forcefully focussed on the fact that her hands never tremble, even when she is in the thralls of a panic. Well, actually they do tremble - but never when it matters. She is supposed to be a strong female character, and there is certainly promise there, but it's so poorly rendered as to almost be negligible.<br />The other characters fall just as flat, and under no circumstance feel as anything other than actors in a particularly uninspired play. Truly, the one even remotely interesting personage was Mr. Berry, for the sole reason of his obstinate adherence to Temperance.<br /><br />The story itself then just sort of peters out once the object everyone has been looking for is found in the most anticlimactic way possible. That the ending is wide open I'll leave to the fact that there are more mysteries in this series, and so the unresolved plotlines will no doubt find some sort of closure in following books. <br /><br />Third person omniscient is a tricky beast, and Phillip Pullman horrendously fails to deliver here. On various occasions the reference to our modern times completely shatters what may have been an immersive tale, had he spent less time physically describing characters (no matter how (un)important to the events at hand) or tipping the reader off on page 9 that the upcoming mystery could have been resolved a lot sooner, and more time thinking his plot through. Overall, he tells rather than shows, and together with his almost stereotypical characters, this makes for a very disappointing read. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18098661051738964349">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_280224279">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280224279" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2950798-maggie-desmond-o-brien" class="left imgcol" title="Maggie Desmond-O'Brien"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1335545360p2/2950798.jpg" alt="Maggie Desmond-O'Brien" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/280224279?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 19, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2950798-maggie-desmond-o-brien" class="user" title="Maggie Desmond-O'Brien">Maggie Desmond-O'Brien</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer280224279">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13235327964125164029">If I had to name a children's/teen's author of the past twenty years most likely to be remembered over the next few centuries, it would have to be J.K. Rowling - it's hard to ignore an author that rewrites an entire culture. If we're talking runners-up, though, it's Philip Pullman hands down. Not only did he write one of the most exquisitely crafted and original fantasy trilogies ever in Northern Lights/The Golden Compass, The Subtle Knife, and The Amber Spyglass, he also has written exquisitely</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13235327964125164029">If I had to name a children's/teen's author of the past twenty years most likely to be remembered over the next few centuries, it would have to be J.K. Rowling - it's hard to ignore an author that rewrites an entire culture. If we're talking runners-up, though, it's Philip Pullman hands down. Not only did he write one of the most exquisitely crafted and original fantasy trilogies ever in Northern Lights/The Golden Compass, The Subtle Knife, and The Amber Spyglass, he also has written exquisitely crafted and original novels pretty much everywhere else. Don't believe me? Check out his Wikipedia bibliography. Despite the incredible variety of his work, from modern-day fairy tales to plays to comics to a kids' activity book titled Using the Oxford Junior Dictionary, he's special in that he never loses his quirky, playful, and eloquent voice - though perhaps it was strained in that last title. <br /><br />Actually, why don't I quit the uber-reviewer jargon and justification and cut to the chase: I am a proud Philip Pullman fangrrl. I'm working on the T-shirts.<br /><br />That's why I'm kind of astonished that I made it through this many years of fandom (eight and counting) without picking up his second most well known series, the Sally Lockhart trilogy - of which The Ruby in the Smoke is the first installment. Unlike 95.1% of the time (very scientific statistic there), I didn't have the excuse that I was broke and couldn't get a copy, because my parents were nice enough to stick it in my Santa stocking the Christmas I was nine years old. I seriously have no idea how a book by an author I love manages to kick around my bookshelves for almost seven years without being read or lost or both, but this one managed it, and in hindsight maybe that's not terrible. While this book wasn't quite on par with Lyra and Will and company, I still have a whole new set of characters to fall in love with.<br /><br />First of all, Sally is a bad@$$ - capable, smart, and no-nonsense - but she's also not perfect. She gets in over her head, is bossy, definitely not great with kids, and sometimes she gets downright freaked - just like a real sixteen-year-old. (A side note for fellow Doctor Who fans, Billie Piper got the role in a 2007 TV movie adaptation.) Rosa and Frederick are delightfully boho-ditzy-artist types, while the ensemble is sinister and entertaining by turns. The setting of grimy, pea-soup-foggy London is so vivid it's almost a character in and of itself, full of opium dens and seedy alleyways and big-eyed orphans. If you're not already a convert to the steampunk/Victorian scene it might make for heavy going, but for addicts like me it's a heady thing.<br /><br />The thing I loved the most about it is the sensation that not one word is wasted - it's a short, small read, perfect purse-size. Pullman is a master at sucking you in without draining you, something I'm only truly starting to appreciate three weeks into spring semester. After school and homework I'm exhausted and cranky, and all I want is a book that will entertain me and distract me from that hideously difficult Comp II assignment that's due tomorrow, while also being well-written enough that the literary snob in me doesn't fall into a saccharine coma. The Ruby in the Smoke fits that bill perfectly, and I can't wait to pick up the sequels. Philip Pullman, you're still my hero! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13235327964125164029">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer186632907">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17818114335814125835">I listened to my first audio book recently 'The Agency: A Spy in the House' by Y.S. Lee, which I enjoyed. A friend recommended 'The Ruby in the Smoke' by Philip Pullman, she said there were some similarities between the two stories and she thought I would enjoy Pullman's book as well. <br /><br />'The Ruby in the Smoke' was more a more sophisticated story with better developed characters. Opium use and addiction factor into the story and there are several murders and scenes with violence which might frighte</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17818114335814125835">I listened to my first audio book recently 'The Agency: A Spy in the House' by Y.S. Lee, which I enjoyed. A friend recommended 'The Ruby in the Smoke' by Philip Pullman, she said there were some similarities between the two stories and she thought I would enjoy Pullman's book as well. <br /><br />'The Ruby in the Smoke' was more a more sophisticated story with better developed characters. Opium use and addiction factor into the story and there are several murders and scenes with violence which might frighten some readers. The violence was not particularly graphic, just frightening, which in my opinion only added to the suspense of the story. <br /><br />I liked the mystery and the protagonist Sally Lockhart, as well as the friends she makes along the way and I thought the solution to the mystery surrounding the ruby was interesting. <br /><br />Listening to an audio book is a very different thing than reading a book for me. When I'm reading I generally make notes and write down character's names and dates that events happen to help me figure out what's going on and what might be potential motivations and how much time elapsed between certain events. Listening alone without the written word in front of me to help cement in my mind dates and names was a different experience. Listening to this while driving added another challenge, I found that if my mind wandered away from the story the least little bit I would have to go back and replay what I missed incase it was something vital to the story. As it was I didn't figure anything out I just listened and enjoyed the ride. <br /><br />I loved Anton Lesser's performance, he is a fabulous actor/reader and added a layer of richness that I wouldn't have had if I had read the printed page instead of listening to the audio version. His voices for all of the characters are fabulous. I would recommend this to listeners of many ages not just the Young Adult audience it is intended for. <br /><br />10/2/2014: I just finished listening to this again and I loved it just as much as I did the first time, maybe more because I could appreciate Pullman's writing in a way I couldn't the first time because I was so engrossed in the action of the story. I highly recommend this series, I just love these characters.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17818114335814125835">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1314209261425114006">Philip Pullman's 'Ruby in the Smoke' is an exciting tale of drama and mystery that will leave you in complete suspense and sitting on the edge of your seat with tense aprehension. I thoroughly enjoyed Philip Pulman's 'His Dark Materials' trilogy but was disapointed to thus find that the rest of his works were less adviertised or publisised, as they in my mind are just as great too. This particular novel i took much pleasure and enjoyment from reading hence i was unable to put it down, as i was l</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1314209261425114006">Philip Pullman's 'Ruby in the Smoke' is an exciting tale of drama and mystery that will leave you in complete suspense and sitting on the edge of your seat with tense aprehension. I thoroughly enjoyed Philip Pulman's 'His Dark Materials' trilogy but was disapointed to thus find that the rest of his works were less adviertised or publisised, as they in my mind are just as great too. This particular novel i took much pleasure and enjoyment from reading hence i was unable to put it down, as i was lost within a compelling adventure that was dark and brimmed full of danger. The main character Sally Lockheart is one whom i admired greatly and which placed within the backdrop of Victorian London made this tale apsolutely perfect, and one which was utterly realistic and authentic with the edition of innumerable descriptions on all the spectacular details of this specific era that Philip Pullman included. It contained much human corruption within a sinister backdop of the murderous London Opium traders, whilst also debating upon the lengths that civilians might go to when it comes to juggling life &amp; death; you only have to mention as a concequence to me the 'seven blessings' and since having read this novel chills go down my spine. It was a read that i found thoroughly engaging, captivating and mesmirisingly curious. It encapsulates all the social deprevation, hardships and human suffering that one could encounter in Victorian London, which transports you back in time to an era of clouded mystery and hidden clues. I travelled on a rollercoaster of an adventure until it came to an aprupt end, with which by now i was utterly captivated by the storyline and the characters and iching for a conclusion. To those readers who enjoy mystery novels, crime, thriller or enjoy works such as 'His Dark Materials' by Philip Pullman or 'Sherlock Holmes' by Sir Arthur Conan Doyal then this particular tale will not disapoint but rather triumph spectacularly. </span>
